      <p>
       <b>
        PJSC Aeroflot – Russian Airlines
       </b>
       (Russian:
       <span lang="ru" xml:lang="ru">
        ПАО "Аэрофло́т — Росси́йские авиали́нии"
       </span>
       ,
       <i lang="ru-Latn" title="Russian-language transliteration" xml:lang="ru-Latn">
        PAO Aeroflot—Rossiyskiye avialinii
       </i>
       ) (
       <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Exchange" title="Moscow Exchange">
        MCX
       </a>
       :
       <a class="external text" href="http://moex.com/en/issue.aspx?code=AFLT" rel="nofollow">
        AFLT
       </a>
       ), commonly known as
       <b>
        Aeroflot
       </b>
       (
       <span class="nowrap">
        <small>
         English:
        </small>
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="/ɛər/: 'are' in 'bare'">
            ɛər
           </span>
           <span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">
            oʊ
           </span>
           <span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">
            ˌ
           </span>
           <span title="'f' in 'find'">
            f
           </span>
           <span title="'l' in 'lie'">
            l
           </span>
           <span title="/ɒ/: 'o' in 'body'">
            ɒ
           </span>
           <span title="'t' in 'tie'">
            t
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       or
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">
            ˌ
           </span>
           <span title="/ɛər/: 'are' in 'bare'">
            ɛər
           </span>
           <span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">
            oʊ
           </span>
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'f' in 'find'">
            f
           </span>
           <span title="'l' in 'lie'">
            l
           </span>
           <span title="/ɒ/: 'o' in 'body'">
            ɒ
           </span>
           <span title="'t' in 'tie'">
            t
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
        <small class="nowrap">
         (
         <span class="unicode haudio">
          <span class="fn">
           <span style="white-space:nowrap">
            <a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Aeroflot_from_Russia_pronunciation_(Voice_of_America).ogg" title="About this sound">
             <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
            </a>
           </span>
           <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c9/En-us-Aeroflot_from_Russia_pronunciation_%28Voice_of_America%29.ogg" title="En-us-Aeroflot from Russia pronunciation (Voice of America).ogg">
            listen
           </a>
          </span>
         </span>
         )
        </small>
       </span>
       ) (Russian:
       <span lang="ru" xml:lang="ru">
        Аэрофлот
       </span>
       , English translation: "air fleet",
       <small>
        pronounced
       </small>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Russian" title="Help:IPA/Russian">
         [ɐɛrɐˈfɫot]
        </a>
       </span>
       ), is the
       <a href="/wiki/Flag_carrier" title="Flag carrier">
        flag carrier
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_cancels_eight_A350-800s_3-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_cancels_eight_A350-800s-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and largest airline of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Federation" title="Russian Federation">
        Russian Federation
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Russia’s_Aeroflot_to_acquire_Transaero_Airlines_4-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Russia’s_Aeroflot_to_acquire_Transaero_Airlines-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Air_carrier" title="Air carrier">
        carrier
       </a>
       is an
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Open_joint_stock_company" title="Open joint stock company">
        open joint stock company
       </a>
       that operates domestic and international passenger and services, mainly from its
       <a href="/wiki/Airline_hub" title="Airline hub">
        hub
       </a>
       at
       <a href="/wiki/Sheremetyevo_International_Airport" title="Sheremetyevo International Airport">
        Sheremetyevo International Airport
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Aeroflot is one of the
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_airlines_by_foundation_date" title="List of airlines by foundation date">
        oldest airlines
       </a>
       in the world, tracing its history back to 1923. During the Soviet era, Aeroflot was the Soviet
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_airline" title="National airline">
        national airline
       </a>
       and the largest airline in the world.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lcweb2.loc.gov_5-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-lcweb2.loc.gov-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Smith_6-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Smith-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Following the
       <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">
        dissolution of the USSR
       </a>
       , the carrier has been transformed from a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_Enterprise" title="State Enterprise">
        state-run enterprise
       </a>
       into a semi-privatised company which ranked 19th most profitable airline in the world in 2007.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Russia’s_Aeroflot_Ranked_Close_to_World_Best_Airlines_7-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Russia’s_Aeroflot_Ranked_Close_to_World_Best_Airlines-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Aeroflot is still considered the
       <i>
        de facto
       </i>
       national airline of Russia.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aircraft_Briefs-Dec._5,_2017_8-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aircraft_Briefs-Dec._5,_2017-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is 51%-owned by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Government" title="Russian Government">
        Russian Government
       </a>
       . As of September 2013
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Aeroflot&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , the Aeroflot Group had 30,328 employees.
      </p>
      <p>
       The company has embarked on a fleet modernisation programme, extensive route restructuring, and an image overhaul. The airline joined
       <a href="/wiki/SkyTeam" title="SkyTeam">
        SkyTeam
       </a>
       in April 2006, becoming the 10th member of the
       <a href="/wiki/Airline_alliance" title="Airline alliance">
        alliance
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>
      <div class="toc" id="toc">

      <p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Aeroflot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history_of_Soviet_civil_aviation">
        Early history of Soviet civil aviation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Aeroflot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early history of Soviet civil aviation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:History_Aeroflot_Dobrolet.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3330" data-file-width="2239" height="253" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/History_Aeroflot_Dobrolet.jpg/170px-History_Aeroflot_Dobrolet.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/History_Aeroflot_Dobrolet.jpg/255px-History_Aeroflot_Dobrolet.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/History_Aeroflot_Dobrolet.jpg/340px-History_Aeroflot_Dobrolet.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:History_Aeroflot_Dobrolet.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         An early Soviet poster calling on citizens to buy stock in
         <a href="/wiki/Dobrolyot" title="Dobrolyot">
          Dobrolyot
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       On 17 January 1921, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sovnarkom" title="Sovnarkom">
        Sovnarkom
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic" title="Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic">
        Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic
       </a>
       published
       <i>
        "About Air Transportation"
       </i>
       . The document signed by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lenin" title="Lenin">
        Lenin
       </a>
       set out the basic regulations on
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Air_transport" title="Air transport">
        air transport
       </a>
       over the territory of the RSFSR. The document was significant as it was the first time that a Russian state had declared sovereignty over its
       <a href="/wiki/Airspace" title="Airspace">
        airspace
       </a>
       . In addition, the document defined rules for the operation of foreign aircraft over the Soviet Union's airspace and territory. After Lenin issued an order, a State Commission was formed on 31 January 1921 for the purpose of civil aviation planning in the Soviet Union. As a result of the commission's plans, Glavvozdukhflot (Chief Administration of the Civil Air Fleet) (Russian:
       <span lang="ru" xml:lang="ru">
        Главвоздухфлот (Главное управление воздушного флота)
       </span>
       ) was established, and it began mail and passenger flights on the Moscow-
       <a href="/wiki/Oryol" title="Oryol">
        Oryol
       </a>
       -
       <a href="/wiki/Kursk" title="Kursk">
        Kursk
       </a>
       -
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kharkov" title="Kharkov">
        Kharkov
       </a>
       route on 1 May 1921 using
       <a href="/wiki/Sikorsky_Ilya_Muromets" title="Sikorsky Ilya Muromets">
        Sikorsky Ilya Muromets
       </a>
       aircraft.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hugh_9-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-hugh-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         1
        </span>
       </sup>
       This was followed by the formation of
       <a href="/wiki/Deruluft" title="Deruluft">
        Deruluft-Deutsch Russische Luftverkehrs A.G.
       </a>
       in Berlin on 11 November 1921, as a joint venture between the Soviet Union and Germany. The company, whose aircraft were registered in both Germany and the Soviet Union, began operations on 1 May 1922 with a
       <a href="/wiki/Fokker_F.III" title="Fokker F.III">
        Fokker F.III
       </a>
       flying between
       <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6nigsberg" title="Königsberg">
        Königsberg
       </a>
       and Moscow.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hugh_9-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-hugh-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         2
        </span>
       </sup>
       The service was initially operated twice a week and restricted to the carriage of mail.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hugh_9-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-hugh-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         2–3
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On 3 February 1923 Sovnarkom approved plans for the expansion of the Red Air Fleet, and it is this date which was officially recognised as the beginning of
       <a href="/wiki/Civil_aviation" title="Civil aviation">
        civil aviation
       </a>
       in the Soviet Union. After a resolution of the
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Committee_of_the_Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Central Committee of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union">
        Central Committee of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union
       </a>
       , the Enterprise for Friends of the Air Fleet (ODVF) was founded on 8 March 1923, followed by the formation of
       <a href="/wiki/Dobrolyot" title="Dobrolyot">
        Dobrolet
       </a>
       (Russian:
       <span lang="ru" xml:lang="ru">
        Добролёт
       </span>
       ) on 17 March 1923. The artist
       <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Rodchenko" title="Alexander Rodchenko">
        Alexander Rodchenko
       </a>
       became involved in the ODVF at this time. He designed posters encouraging citizens to buy stock in Dobrolet and the famous "Winged Hammer and Sickle" logo still used by Aeroflot.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Regular flights by Dobrolet from Moscow to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nizhniy_Novgorod" title="Nizhniy Novgorod">
        Nizhniy Novgorod
       </a>
       commenced on 15 July 1923. During the same period, an additional two airlines were established;
       <a href="/wiki/Zakavia" title="Zakavia">
        Zakavia
       </a>
       being based in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tiflis" title="Tiflis">
        Tiflis
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Ukrvozdukhput" title="Ukrvozdukhput">
        Ukrvozdukhput
       </a>
       based in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kharkov" title="Kharkov">
        Kharkov
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hugh_9-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-hugh-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         2
        </span>
       </sup>
       During 1923 an agreement was signed establishing a subdivision of Dobrolet to be based in
       <a href="/wiki/Tashkent" title="Tashkent">
        Tashkent
       </a>
       , which would operate to points in
       <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Central_Asia" title="Soviet Central Asia">
        Soviet Central Asia
       </a>
       . Services between Tashkent and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alma_Ata" title="Alma Ata">
        Alma Ata
       </a>
       began on 27 April 1924, and by the end of 1924 the subdivision had carried 480 passengers and 500 kilograms (1,100 lb) of mail and freight, on a total of 210 flights.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hugh_9-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-hugh-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         6
        </span>
       </sup>
       In March 1924, Dobrolet began operating flights from
       <a href="/wiki/Sevastopol" title="Sevastopol">
        Sevastopol
       </a>
       to
       <a href="/wiki/Yalta" title="Yalta">
        Yalta
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yevpatoriya" title="Yevpatoriya">
        Yevpatoriya
       </a>
       in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crimean_Peninsula" title="Crimean Peninsula">
        Crimea
       </a>
       . Dobrolet's route network was extended during the 1925–1927 period to include
       <a href="/wiki/Kazan" title="Kazan">
        Kazan
       </a>
       and regular flights between Moscow and Kharkov were inaugurated. Plans were made for Dobrolet flights to Kharkov to connect with Ukrvozdukhput services to
       <a href="/wiki/Kiev" title="Kiev">
        Kiev
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Odessa" title="Odessa">
        Odessa
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Rostov-on-Don" title="Rostov-on-Don">
        Rostov-on-Don
       </a>
       . During 1925, Dobrolet operated 2,000 flights over a distance of 1,000,000 kilometres (620,000 mi), carrying 14,000 passengers and 127,500 kilograms (281,100 lb) of freight, on a route network extending to some 5,000 kilometres (3,100 mi).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hugh_9-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-hugh-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         7
        </span>
       </sup>
       Dobrolet was transformed from a Russian to an all-Union enterprise on 21 September 1926 as a result of Sovnarkom resolutions, and in 1928 Dobrolet was merged with Ukrvozdukhput; the latter having merged with Zakavia in 1925.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hugh_9-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-hugh-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         6–7
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Formative_years">
        Formative years
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Aeroflot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Formative years">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aeroflot_ANT-20bis.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="732" data-file-width="1200" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Aeroflot_ANT-20bis.jpg/220px-Aeroflot_ANT-20bis.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Aeroflot_ANT-20bis.jpg/330px-Aeroflot_ANT-20bis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Aeroflot_ANT-20bis.jpg/440px-Aeroflot_ANT-20bis.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aeroflot_ANT-20bis.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tupolev_ANT-20bis" title="Tupolev ANT-20bis">
          Tupolev ANT-20bis
         </a>
         was used for cargo flights from Moscow to
         <a href="/wiki/Mineralnye_Vody" title="Mineralnye Vody">
          Mineralnye Vody
         </a>
         before World War II
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Responsibility for all civil aviation activities in the Soviet Union came under the control of the Chief Directorate of the Civil Air Fleet on 25 February 1932, and on 25 March 1932 the name "Aeroflot" was officially adopted for the entire Soviet Civil Air Fleet.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hugh_9-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-hugh-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         10
        </span>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Communist Party of the Soviet Union">
        Communist Party of the Soviet Union
       </a>
       Congress in 1933 set out development plans for the civil aviation industry for the following five years, which would see air transportation becoming one of the primary means of transportation in the Soviet Union, linking all major cities. The government also implemented plans to expand the Soviet aircraft industry to make it less dependent on foreign built aircraft;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hugh_9-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-hugh-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         10–11
        </span>
       </sup>
       in 1930 some fifty percent of aircraft flying services in the Soviet Union were of foreign manufacture.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hugh_9-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-hugh-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         8
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Expansion of air routes which had taken shape in the late 1920s,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hugh_9-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-hugh-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         8
        </span>
       </sup>
       continued into the 1930s. Local (MVL) services were greatly expanded in Soviet Central Asia and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soviet_Far_East" title="Soviet Far East">
        Soviet Far East
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hugh_9-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-hugh-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         11–13
        </span>
       </sup>
       which by the end of the second
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Five-Year_Plans_for_the_National_Economy_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Five-Year Plans for the National Economy of the Soviet Union">
        Five-Year Plan
       </a>
       in 1937 was 35,000 kilometres (22,000 mi) in length out of a total network of some 93,300 kilometres (58,000 mi).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hugh_9-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-hugh-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         13
        </span>
       </sup>
       The agreement between the Soviet Union and Germany relating to Deruluft expired on 1 January 1937 and wasn't renewed, which saw the joint venture carrier ceasing operations on 1 April 1937. On that date Aeroflot began operations on the Moscow to
       <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">
        Stockholm
       </a>
       route, and began operating the ex-Deruluft route from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leningrad" title="Leningrad">
        Leningrad
       </a>
       to
       <a href="/wiki/Riga" title="Riga">
        Riga
       </a>
       utilising
       <a href="/wiki/Douglas_DC-3" title="Douglas DC-3">
        Douglas DC-3s
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Tupolev_ANT-35" title="Tupolev ANT-35">
        Tupolev ANT-35s
       </a>
       (PS-35s). Flights from Moscow to Berlin, via Königsberg, were suspended until 1940, when they were restarted by Aeroflot and
       <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">
        Lufthansa
       </a>
       as a result of the signing of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Molotov-Ribbentrop_Pact" title="Molotov-Ribbentrop Pact">
        Molotov-Ribbentrop Pact
       </a>
       , and would continue until the beginning of the
       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_II)" title="Eastern Front (World War II)">
        Great Patriotic War
       </a>
       in 1941.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hugh_9-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-hugh-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         5
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ps-84-nowarra135.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="481" data-file-width="800" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Ps-84-nowarra135.jpg/220px-Ps-84-nowarra135.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Ps-84-nowarra135.jpg/330px-Ps-84-nowarra135.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Ps-84-nowarra135.jpg/440px-Ps-84-nowarra135.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ps-84-nowarra135.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         An Aeroflot PS-84 (a
         <a href="/wiki/Douglas_DC-3" title="Douglas DC-3">
          Douglas DC-3
         </a>
         , modified by fitment of Soviet engines) at Moscow City Airport in 1940. The
         <a href="/wiki/Lisunov_Li-2" title="Lisunov Li-2">
          Lisunov Li-2
         </a>
         , a license-built version of the DC-3, would become the backbone of the fleet after the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Patriotic_War" title="Great Patriotic War">
          Great Patriotic War
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Under the third Five-Year Plan, which began in 1938, civil aviation development continued, with improvements to airport installations being made and construction of airports being commenced. In addition to the expansion of services between the Soviet Union's main cities, local routes (MVL) were also expanded, and by 1940, some 337 MVL routes saw operations on a scheduled basis. Serial production of the
       <a href="/wiki/Lisunov_Li-2" title="Lisunov Li-2">
        Lisunov Li-2
       </a>
       (license-built Douglas DC-3) commenced in 1939, and the aircraft became the backbone of Aeroflot's fleet on mainline trunk routes. When the
       <a href="/wiki/Operation_Barbarossa" title="Operation Barbarossa">
        Soviet Union was invaded
       </a>
       by
       <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">
        Nazi Germany
       </a>
       on 22 June 1941, the following day the Sovnarkom placed the Civil Air Fleet under the control of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Narkomat" title="Narkomat">
        Narkomat
       </a>
       , leading to the full-scale mobilisation of Aeroflot crews and technicians for the Soviet war effort. Prior to the invasion, the Aeroflot network extended over some 146,000 kilometres (91,000 mi), and amongst the longest routes being operated from Moscow were those to
       <a href="/wiki/Tbilisi" title="Tbilisi">
        Tbilisi
       </a>
       (via
       <a href="/wiki/Baku" title="Baku">
        Baku
       </a>
       ), Tashkent and
       <a href="/wiki/Vladivostok" title="Vladivostok">
        Vladivostok
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hugh_9-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-hugh-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         13
        </span>
       </sup>
       Aeroflot aircraft, including PS-35s and PS-43s, were based at Moscow's
       <a href="/wiki/Khodynka_Aerodrome" title="Khodynka Aerodrome">
        Central Airport
       </a>
       ; and important missions undertaken by Aeroflot aircraft and crews included flying supplies to the besieged cities of Leningrad, Kiev, Odessa and Sevastopol.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hugh_9-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-hugh-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         14
        </span>
       </sup>
       During the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Stalingrad" title="Battle of Stalingrad">
        Battle of Stalingrad
       </a>
       , between August 1942 and February 1943, Aeroflot operated 46,000 missions to Stalingrad, ferrying in 2,587 tonnes (5,703,000 lb) of supplies and some 30,000 troops. Following the defeat of the
       <a href="/wiki/Wehrmacht" title="Wehrmacht">
        Wehrmacht
       </a>
       , some 80
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Junkers_Ju-52" title="Junkers Ju-52">
        Junkers Ju-52/3ms
       </a>
       were captured from the Germans, and were placed into the service of the Civil Air Fleet, and after the war were placed into regular service across the Soviet Union.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hugh_9-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-hugh-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         15
        </span>
       </sup>
       Whilst civil operations in
       <a href="/wiki/European_Russia" title="European Russia">
        European Russia
       </a>
       west of the front line, which ran from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leningrad" title="Leningrad">
        Leningrad
       </a>
       to Moscow to
       <a href="/wiki/Rostov-on-Don" title="Rostov-on-Don">
        Rostov-on-Don
       </a>
       , were prevented from operating because of the war, services from Moscow to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urals" title="Urals">
        Urals
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">
        Siberia
       </a>
       , Central Asia, and other regions which were not affected by the war, continued.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hugh_9-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-hugh-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         15–16
        </span>
       </sup>
       By the end of the war, Aeroflot had flown 1,595,943 special missions, including 83,782 at night, and carried 1,538,982 men and 122,027 tonnes (269,023,000 lb) of cargo.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hugh_9-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-hugh-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         16
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Post-World_War_II_operations">
        Post-World War II operations
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Aeroflot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Post-World War II operations">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aeroflot_Ilyushin_Il-14_at_Arlanda,_November_1970.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1086" data-file-width="1593" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Aeroflot_Ilyushin_Il-14_at_Arlanda%2C_November_1970.jpg/220px-Aeroflot_Ilyushin_Il-14_at_Arlanda%2C_November_1970.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Aeroflot_Ilyushin_Il-14_at_Arlanda%2C_November_1970.jpg/330px-Aeroflot_Ilyushin_Il-14_at_Arlanda%2C_November_1970.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Aeroflot_Ilyushin_Il-14_at_Arlanda%2C_November_1970.jpg/440px-Aeroflot_Ilyushin_Il-14_at_Arlanda%2C_November_1970.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aeroflot_Ilyushin_Il-14_at_Arlanda,_November_1970.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         After its introduction in 1954, the
         <a href="/wiki/Ilyushin_Il-14" title="Ilyushin Il-14">
          Ilyushin Il-14
         </a>
         operated on Aeroflot's All-Union services.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       At the end of World War II, the
       <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Government of the Soviet Union">
        Soviet government
       </a>
       went about repairing and rebuilding essential airport infrastructure, and it strengthened the Aeroflot units in the European part of the Soviet Union. Aeroflot had by the end of 1945 carried 537,000 passengers, compared with 359,000 in 1940.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hugh_9-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-hugh-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         16
        </span>
       </sup>
       The government made it a priority in the immediate postwar years to expand services from Moscow to the capital of the
       <a href="/wiki/Republics_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Republics of the Soviet Union">
        Union republics
       </a>
       , in addition to important industrial centres on the country. To enable this, the government transferred to Aeroflot a large number of
       <a href="/wiki/Lisunov_Li-2" title="Lisunov Li-2">
        Lisunov Li-2s
       </a>
       , and they would become the backbone of the fleet.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hugh_9-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-hugh-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         17
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Ilyushin_Il-12" title="Ilyushin Il-12">
        Ilyushin Il-12
       </a>
       entered service on Aeroflot's all-Union scheduled routes on 22 August 1947, and supplemented already existing Li-2 services. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ilyushin_Il-18_(1947)" title="Ilyushin Il-18 (1947)">
        original Ilyushin Il-18
       </a>
       entered service around the same time as the Il-12, and was operated on routes from Moscow to
       <a href="/wiki/Yakutsk" title="Yakutsk">
        Yakutsk
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Khabarovsk" title="Khabarovsk">
        Khabarovsk
       </a>
       , Vladivostok, Alma Ata, Tashkent,
       <a href="/wiki/Sochi" title="Sochi">
        Sochi
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mineralnye_Vody" title="Mineralnye Vody">
        Mineralnye Vody
       </a>
       and Tbilisi. By 1950 the Il-18 was withdrawn from service, being replaced by Il-12s.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hugh_9-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-hugh-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         18,20
        </span>
       </sup>
       MVL and
       <a href="/wiki/General_aviation" title="General aviation">
        general aviation
       </a>
       services received a boost in March 1948, when the first
       <a href="/wiki/Antonov_An-2" title="Antonov An-2">
        Antonov An-2s
       </a>
       were delivered and entered service in Central Russia. Development of MVL services over latter years was attributed to the An-2, which was operated by Aeroflot in all areas of the Soviet Union.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hugh_9-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-hugh-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         20
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Aeroflot's route network had extended to 295,400 kilometres (183,600 mi) by 1950, and it carried 1,603,700 passengers, 151,070 tonnes (333,050,000 lb) of freight and 30,580 tonnes (67,420,000 lb) of mail during the same year. Night flights began in the same year, and the 5th Five-Year Plan, covering the period 1951–1955, emphasised Aeroflot expanding night-time operations, which vastly improved aircraft utilisation. By 1952, some 700 destinations around the Soviet Union received regular flights from Aeroflot.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hugh_9-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-hugh-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         20
        </span>
       </sup>
       On 30 November 1954, the
       <a href="/wiki/Ilyushin_Il-14" title="Ilyushin Il-14">
        Ilyushin Il-14
       </a>
       entered service, and the aircraft took a leading role in the operation of Aeroflot's all-Union services. The number of passengers carried in 1955 increased to 2,500,000, whilst freight and mail carriage also increased, to 194,960 and 63,760 tons, respectively. By this time, Aeroflot's route network covered a distance of some 321,500 kilometres (199,800 mi).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hugh_9-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-hugh-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         21
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aeroflot_Tupolev_Tu-104B_at_Arlanda,_July_1972.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2452" data-file-width="3864" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Aeroflot_Tupolev_Tu-104B_at_Arlanda%2C_July_1972.jpg/220px-Aeroflot_Tupolev_Tu-104B_at_Arlanda%2C_July_1972.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Aeroflot_Tupolev_Tu-104B_at_Arlanda%2C_July_1972.jpg/330px-Aeroflot_Tupolev_Tu-104B_at_Arlanda%2C_July_1972.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Aeroflot_Tupolev_Tu-104B_at_Arlanda%2C_July_1972.jpg/440px-Aeroflot_Tupolev_Tu-104B_at_Arlanda%2C_July_1972.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aeroflot_Tupolev_Tu-104B_at_Arlanda,_July_1972.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Aeroflot became the first airline in the world with sustained jet aircraft service, when it introduced the
         <a href="/wiki/Tupolev_Tu-104" title="Tupolev Tu-104">
          Tupolev Tu-104
         </a>
         in 1956.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/20th_Congress_of_the_Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="20th Congress of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union">
        20th Communist Party Congress
       </a>
       , held in 1956, saw plans for Aeroflot services to be dramatically increased. The airline would see its overall activities increased from its then current levels by 3.8 times, and it was set the target of the carriage of 16,000,000 passengers by 1960. In order to meet these goals, Aeroflot introduced higher capacity turbojet and turbine-prop aircraft on key domestic routes, and on services to Aeroflot destinations abroad. A major step for Aeroflot occurred on 15 September 1956 when the
       <a href="/wiki/Tupolev_Tu-104" title="Tupolev Tu-104">
        Tupolev Tu-104
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Jet_aircraft" title="Jet aircraft">
        jet airliner
       </a>
       entered service on the Moscow-
       <a href="/wiki/Omsk" title="Omsk">
        Omsk
       </a>
       -
       <a href="/wiki/Irkutsk" title="Irkutsk">
        Irkutsk
       </a>
       route, marking the world's first sustained jet airline service. The airline began international flights with the type on 12 October 1956 under the command of
       <a href="/wiki/Boris_Bugayev" title="Boris Bugayev">
        Boris Bugayev
       </a>
       with flights from Moscow to
       <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">
        Prague
       </a>
       . The aircraft placed Aeroflot in an enviable position, as airlines in the West had operated throughout the 1950s with large piston-engined aircraft.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hugh_9-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-hugh-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         21
        </span>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-davies_11-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-davies-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         44
        </span>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By 1958 the route network covered 349,200 kilometres (217,000 mi), and the airline carried 8,231,500 passengers, and 445,600 tons of mail and freight, with fifteen percent of all-Union services being operated by jet aircraft.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hugh_9-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-hugh-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         23
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Aeroflot introduced the
       <a href="/wiki/Antonov_An-10" title="Antonov An-10">
        Antonov An-10
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Ilyushin_Il-18" title="Ilyushin Il-18">
        Ilyushin Il-18
       </a>
       in 1959, and together with its existing jet aircraft, the airline was able to extend services on modern aircraft to twenty one cities during 1960.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hugh_9-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-hugh-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         23
        </span>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Tupolev_Tu-114" title="Tupolev Tu-114">
        Tupolev Tu-114
       </a>
       , then the world's largest airliner, entered service with the Soviet carrier on 24 April 1961 on the Moscow-
       <a href="/wiki/Khabarovsk" title="Khabarovsk">
        Khabarovsk
       </a>
       route; covering a distance of 6,980 kilometres (4,340 mi) in 8 hours 20 minutes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hugh_9-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-hugh-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         24
        </span>
       </sup>
       The expansion of the Aeroflot fleet saw services with modern aircraft being extended to forty one cities in 1961, with fifty percent of all-Union services being operated by these aircraft. This fleet expansion also saw the number of passengers carried in 1961 skyrocketing to 21,800,000.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hugh_9-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-hugh-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         24
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aeroflot_Yakovlev_Yak-40_in_Sweden.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1081" data-file-width="1597" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Aeroflot_Yakovlev_Yak-40_in_Sweden.jpg/220px-Aeroflot_Yakovlev_Yak-40_in_Sweden.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Aeroflot_Yakovlev_Yak-40_in_Sweden.jpg/330px-Aeroflot_Yakovlev_Yak-40_in_Sweden.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Aeroflot_Yakovlev_Yak-40_in_Sweden.jpg/440px-Aeroflot_Yakovlev_Yak-40_in_Sweden.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aeroflot_Yakovlev_Yak-40_in_Sweden.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Aeroflot became the first airline to operate the first
         <a href="/wiki/Regional_jet" title="Regional jet">
          regional jet
         </a>
         , the
         <a href="/wiki/Yakovlev_Yak-40" title="Yakovlev Yak-40">
          Yakovlev Yak-40
         </a>
         , in 1968.
         <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
          [
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
            <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2011)">
             citation needed
            </span>
           </a>
          </i>
          ]
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Further expansion came in 1962 when both the
       <a href="/wiki/Tupolev_Tu-124" title="Tupolev Tu-124">
        Tupolev Tu-124
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Antonov_An-24" title="Antonov An-24">
        Antonov An-24
       </a>
       entered regular service with Aeroflot on various medium and short-haul routes. By 1964, Aeroflot operated direct flights from Moscow to 100 cities, from Leningrad to 44 cities, and from Kiev to 38 cities. The airline also operated direct flights from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mineralnyie_Vody" title="Mineralnyie Vody">
        Mineralnyie Vody
       </a>
       to 48 cities across the Soviet Union, denoting the importance of the operation of holiday aircraft services to Aeroflot.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hugh_9-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-hugh-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         26
        </span>
       </sup>
       Statistics for the same year showed Aerfolot operating an all-Union route network extending over 400,000 kilometres (250,000 mi), and carrying 36,800,000 passengers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hugh_9-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-hugh-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         27
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       By 1966 Aeroflot carried 47,200,000 passengers over a domestic route network of 474,600 kilometres (294,900 mi). For the period of the 8th Five-Year Plan, which ran from 1966–1970, Aeroflot carried a total of 302,200,000 passengers, 6.47 billion tons of freight and 1.63 billion tons of mail.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hugh_9-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-hugh-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         27
        </span>
       </sup>
       During the Five-Year Plan period, all-Union services were extended over an additional 350 routes; an additional 1,000 MVL routes were begun, and 40 new routes were opened up with all-cargo flights.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hugh_9-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-hugh-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         27–28
        </span>
       </sup>
       The year 1967 saw the introduction into service of the
       <a href="/wiki/Ilyushin_Il-62" title="Ilyushin Il-62">
        Ilyushin Il-62
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Tupolev_Tu-134" title="Tupolev Tu-134">
        Tupolev Tu-134
       </a>
       , and in September 1968 the
       <a href="/wiki/Yakovlev_Yak-40" title="Yakovlev Yak-40">
        Yakovlev Yak-40
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Regional_jet" title="Regional jet">
        regional jet
       </a>
       began operations on short-haul services. By 1970, the last year of the Five-Year Plan period, Aeroflot was operating flights to over 3,500 destinations in the Soviet Union, and at the height of the 1970 summer holidays season, the airline was carrying approximately 400,000 passengers per day, and some ninety percent of passengers were being carried on propeller-turbine and jet aircraft.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hugh_9-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-hugh-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         28
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Expansion_of_international_flights">
        Expansion of international flights
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Aeroflot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Expansion of international flights">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_Aeroflot.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="750" data-file-width="1500" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Flag_of_the_Aeroflot.svg/220px-Flag_of_the_Aeroflot.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Flag_of_the_Aeroflot.svg/330px-Flag_of_the_Aeroflot.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Flag_of_the_Aeroflot.svg/440px-Flag_of_the_Aeroflot.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_Aeroflot.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Flag of Aeroflot
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In January 1971, the Central Administration of International Air Traffic (Russian:
       <span lang="ru" xml:lang="ru">
        Центральное управление международных воздушных сообщений
       </span>
       ) (TsUMVS) was established within the framework of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IATA" title="IATA">
        IATA
       </a>
       , and became the sole enterprise authorised to operate international flights. Abroad, the airline was known as Aeroflot Soviet Airlines. In 1976, Aeroflot carried its 100 millionth passenger. Its flights were mainly concentrated around the Soviet Union, but the airline also had an international network covering five continents: North and South America, Europe, Africa and Asia. The network included countries such as the United States, Canada, United Kingdom, Spain, Cuba, Mexico and the People's Republic of China.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Aeroflot service between the Soviet Union and the United States was interrupted from 15 September 1983 until 2 August 1990, following an executive order by U.S. President
       <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">
        Ronald Reagan
       </a>
       , revoking the Aeroflot's license to operate flights into and out of the United States following the downing of
       <a href="/wiki/Korean_Air_Lines_Flight_007" title="Korean Air Lines Flight 007">
        Korean Air Lines Flight 007
       </a>
       by the Soviet Air Force. At the start of the 1990s Aeroflot reorganised again giving more autonomy to territorial divisions.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/REG_Davies" title="REG Davies">
        REG Davies
       </a>
       , former curator of the
       <a href="/wiki/Smithsonian_Institution" title="Smithsonian Institution">
        Smithsonian Institution
       </a>
       , claims that by 1992 Aeroflot had over 600,000 people operating over 10,000 aircraft.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-davies_11-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-davies-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         92,94
        </span>
       </sup>
       By 1967, Aeroflot amassed a fleet equal to that of the largest American carriers combined.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Smith_6-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Smith-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_functions">
        Other functions
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Aeroflot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Other functions">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aeroflot_Mil_Mi-10_at_Groningen_Airport.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="683" data-file-width="1024" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Aeroflot_Mil_Mi-10_at_Groningen_Airport.jpg/220px-Aeroflot_Mil_Mi-10_at_Groningen_Airport.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Aeroflot_Mil_Mi-10_at_Groningen_Airport.jpg/330px-Aeroflot_Mil_Mi-10_at_Groningen_Airport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Aeroflot_Mil_Mi-10_at_Groningen_Airport.jpg/440px-Aeroflot_Mil_Mi-10_at_Groningen_Airport.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aeroflot_Mil_Mi-10_at_Groningen_Airport.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         An Aeroflot Mi-10 heavy lift helicopter seen at
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Groningen_Airport" title="Groningen Airport">
          Groningen Airport
         </a>
         in the early 1970s
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Aeroflot also performed other functions, including
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Air_ambulance" title="Air ambulance">
        air ambulance
       </a>
       ;
       <a href="/wiki/Aerial_application" title="Aerial application">
        aerial application
       </a>
       ; heavy lifting for the
       <a href="/wiki/Soviet_space_program" title="Soviet space program">
        Soviet Space Agency
       </a>
       ; offshore oil platform support; exploration and
       <a href="/wiki/Aeromagnetic_survey" title="Aeromagnetic survey">
        aeromagnetic survey
       </a>
       for natural resources; support for construction projects; transport of military troops and supplies (as an adjunct to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soviet_Air_Force" title="Soviet Air Force">
        Soviet Air Force
       </a>
       ); atmospheric research; and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aerial_surveillance" title="Aerial surveillance">
        remote area patrol
       </a>
       . It operated hundreds of helicopters and cargo aircraft in addition to civil airliners. It also operated the Soviet equivalent of a
       <a href="/wiki/Air_transports_of_heads_of_state_and_government" title="Air transports of heads of state and government">
        presidential aircraft
       </a>
       and other VIP transports of government and
       <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Communist Party of the Soviet Union">
        communist party
       </a>
       officials.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lcweb2.loc.gov_5-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-lcweb2.loc.gov-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-davies_11-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-davies-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         94
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Aeroflot was also responsible for such services as ice patrol in the Arctic Ocean and escorting of ships through frozen seas; oil exploration; power line surveillance; and transportation and heavy lifting support on construction projects. For the latter tasks, Aeroflot used, in addition to smaller helicopters, the
       <a href="/wiki/Mil_Mi-10" title="Mil Mi-10">
        Mil Mi-10
       </a>
       flying crane capable of lifting 11,000 to 14,000 kilograms (24,000 to 31,000 lb). Hauling of heavy cargo, including vehicles, was performed by the world's largest operational helicopter, the
       <a href="/wiki/Mil_Mi-26" title="Mil Mi-26">
        Mil Mi-26
       </a>
       . Its unusual eight-blade rotor enabled it to lift a maximum payload of some twenty tons.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lcweb2.loc.gov_5-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-lcweb2.loc.gov-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The medium- and long-range passenger- and cargo aircraft of Aeroflot were also part of the strategic air transport reserve, ready to provide immediate airlift support to the armed forces. Short-range aircraft and helicopters were available for appropriate military support missions.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Post-Soviet_Aeroflot">
        Post-Soviet Aeroflot
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Aeroflot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Post-Soviet Aeroflot">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aeroflot.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="215" data-file-width="600" height="79" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Aeroflot.svg/220px-Aeroflot.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Aeroflot.svg/330px-Aeroflot.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Aeroflot.svg/440px-Aeroflot.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aeroflot.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The "winged
         <a href="/wiki/Hammer_and_sickle" title="Hammer and sickle">
          hammer and sickle
         </a>
         " is the most recognisable symbol of Aeroflot.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In the early 1990s, the Soviet Union underwent massive political upheavals, culminating in the
       <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">
        dissolution of the State
       </a>
       . Former
       <a href="/wiki/Republics_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Republics of the Soviet Union">
        republics of the Soviet Union
       </a>
       declared their independence during January 1990 – December 1991, resulting in the establishment of several independent countries, along with fifteen republics and the
       <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">
        Commonwealth of Independent States
       </a>
       (CIS). Up until that time, Aeroflot had been the only establishment providing air services throughout the Soviet Union, but with its breakup Aeroflot branches of these countries began their own services, and the airline itself came under control of Russia, the largest of the CIS republics, and was renamed
       <i>
        Aeroflot – Russian International Airlines (ARIA)
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hold_the_Jokes,_Please:_Aeroflot_Buffs_Its_Image_14-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Hold_the_Jokes,_Please:_Aeroflot_Buffs_Its_Image-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-With_400_Pieces,_Aeroflot_Is_a_Passenger_Puzzle_15-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-With_400_Pieces,_Aeroflot_Is_a_Passenger_Puzzle-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FI1993_16-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FI1993-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Actually, it was in 1992 that Aeroflot was divided into a number of regional airlines,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Bullish_Bear_17-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-The_Bullish_Bear-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       whereas international routes were operated by ARIA.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FI1993_16-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FI1993-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Smaller regional airlines which emerged from the old Aeroflot were sometimes referred to as
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Babyflot" title="Babyflot">
         Babyflots
        </a>
       </i>
       ;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hold_the_Jokes,_Please:_Aeroflot_Buffs_Its_Image_14-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Hold_the_Jokes,_Please:_Aeroflot_Buffs_Its_Image-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         2
        </span>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/BAL_Bashkirian_Airlines" title="BAL Bashkirian Airlines">
        Bashkirian Airlines
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/KrasAir" title="KrasAir">
        Krasnoyarsk Airlines
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Airways" title="Moscow Airways">
        Moscow Airways
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Tatarstan_Airlines" title="Tatarstan Airlines">
        Tatarstan Airlines
       </a>
       were among the carriers that were formed from former Aeroflot directorates.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-All_Change_at_Aeroflot_18-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-All_Change_at_Aeroflot-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1994, Aeroflot was registered as a
       <a href="/wiki/Joint-stock_company" title="Joint-stock company">
        joint-stock company
       </a>
       and the government sold off 49% of its stake to Aeroflot employees. During the 1990s, Aeroflot was primarily focused on international flights from Moscow. However, by the end of the decade Aeroflot started an expansion in the domestic market. In 2000 the company name was changed to
       <i>
        Aeroflot – Russian Airlines
       </i>
       to reflect the change in the company strategy.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Aeroflot fleet shrank dramatically in the post-Soviet era, dropping from 5,400 planes in 1991 to 115 in 1996.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Since the dissolution, Aeroflot has been actively working towards promoting and redefining itself as a safe and reliable airline.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-A_Face-Lift_for_Down-at-Heel_Aeroflot_21-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-A_Face-Lift_for_Down-at-Heel_Aeroflot-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the early 2000s (decade), the airline hired British consultants for rebranding.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-No_more_service_with_a_scowl_22-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-No_more_service_with_a_scowl-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       From the start, plans were afoot to replace the old Soviet-era
       <a href="/wiki/Hammer_and_sickle" title="Hammer and sickle">
        hammer and sickle
       </a>
       logo, which some people in the West viewed as a reminder of the Soviet communist era; despite this the logo was not scrapped, as it was the most recognisable symbol of the company for over 70 years.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-No_more_service_with_a_scowl_22-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-No_more_service_with_a_scowl-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A new
       <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_livery" title="Aircraft livery">
        livery
       </a>
       and uniforms for flight attendants were designed and a promotional campaign launched in 2003.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aeroflot_A321-200_VP-BWN_SVO_2008-9-15.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="767" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Aeroflot_A321-200_VP-BWN_SVO_2008-9-15.png/220px-Aeroflot_A321-200_VP-BWN_SVO_2008-9-15.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Aeroflot_A321-200_VP-BWN_SVO_2008-9-15.png/330px-Aeroflot_A321-200_VP-BWN_SVO_2008-9-15.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Aeroflot_A321-200_VP-BWN_SVO_2008-9-15.png/440px-Aeroflot_A321-200_VP-BWN_SVO_2008-9-15.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aeroflot_A321-200_VP-BWN_SVO_2008-9-15.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A new
         <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A321" title="Airbus A321">
          Airbus A321
         </a>
         holds for departure whilst an
         <a href="/wiki/Ilyushin_Il-96" title="Ilyushin Il-96">
          Ilyushin Il-96
         </a>
         lands at Aeroflot's
         <a href="/wiki/Sheremetyevo_International_Airport" title="Sheremetyevo International Airport">
          Moscow-Sheremetyevo hub
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Its fleet has undergone a major reorganisation during which most of the Soviet aircraft were replaced by Western-built jets; costs over fuel consumption rather than safety concerns were cited for such a movement.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_Sheds_Its_Soviet_Legacy_and_Turns_to_a_Western_Fleet_24-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_Sheds_Its_Soviet_Legacy_and_Turns_to_a_Western_Fleet-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A319" title="Airbus A319">
        Airbus A319s
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320_family" title="Airbus A320 family">
        A320s
       </a>
       for short-haul flights in Europe; and
       <a href="/wiki/Boeing_767" title="Boeing 767">
        Boeing 767s
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A330" title="Airbus A330">
        Airbus A330s
       </a>
       for long-haul routes; were gradually incorporated into the fleet. In the spring of 2004 an expansion on the domestic market was undertaken, aiming to gain 30% share by 2010 (as of 2006
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Aeroflot&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       it held approximately 9%). The first task was to outperform
       <a href="/wiki/S7_Airlines" title="S7 Airlines">
        S7 Airlines
       </a>
       , a major rival and the leader in the domestic market. On 29 July 2004 a new corporate slogan was adopted: "Sincerely Yours. Aeroflot".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_new_slogan_25-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_new_slogan-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In April 2006
       <span style="display:none">
        (
        <span class="bday dtstart published updated">
         2006-04
        </span>
        )
       </span>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_joins_SkyTeam_26-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_joins_SkyTeam-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Aeroflot became the tenth airline to join
       <a href="/wiki/SkyTeam" title="SkyTeam">
        SkyTeam
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_Becomes_10th_Airline_to_Join_SkyTeam_27-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_Becomes_10th_Airline_to_Join_SkyTeam-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the first air carrier in the former Soviet Union to do so.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Russia’s_Aeroflot_Ranked_Close_to_World_Best_Airlines_7-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Russia’s_Aeroflot_Ranked_Close_to_World_Best_Airlines-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The company announced its plan to increase cargo operations. It registered the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Aeroflot-Cargo" title="Aeroflot-Cargo">
         Aeroflot-Cargo
        </a>
       </i>
       trademark in 2006.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       During that year Aeroflot carried 7,290,000 passengers and 145,300 tons of mail and cargo
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       to 89 destinations in 47 countries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It saw improvements in its earnings and number of passengers carried. The
       <a href="/wiki/Net_profit" title="Net profit">
        net profit
       </a>
       reached $309.4 million (RUB 7.98 billion) in 2006, a 32.3% increase from 2005 earnings of only $234 million (RUB6.03 billion). The revenue for the same 2005–2006 period rose by 13.5% to reach $2.77 billion with an 8.7% gain in passenger numbers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Aeroflot became the sole shareholder of
       <a href="/wiki/Donavia" title="Donavia">
        Donavia
       </a>
       —a domestic airline then-named
       <i>
        Aeroflot-Don
       </i>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Russia's_Aeroflot-Don_to_rebrand_as_Donavia_32-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Russia's_Aeroflot-Don_to_rebrand_as_Donavia-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       —in December 2006
       <span style="display:none">
        (
        <span class="bday dtstart published updated">
         2006-12
        </span>
        )
       </span>
       , when it boosted its stake in the company from 51% to 100%;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Other_News_-_01/12/2007_33-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Other_News_-_01/12/2007-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       soon afterwards,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aeroflot-Nord" title="Aeroflot-Nord">
        Aeroflot-Nord
       </a>
       was created following the buyout of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arkhangelsk_Airlines" title="Arkhangelsk Airlines">
        Arkhangelsk Airlines
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Arranged_marriages:_Russia_focus_34-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Arranged_marriages:_Russia_focus-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As of March 2007
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Aeroflot&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , Aeroflot was owned by the Russian Government via
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rosimushchestvo" title="Rosimushchestvo">
        Rosimushchestvo
       </a>
       (51.17%), National Reserve Corporation (27%) and employees and others (19%), and has 14,900 employees.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aeroflot_flight_attendant_(hostess).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3972" data-file-width="2680" height="252" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Aeroflot_flight_attendant_%28hostess%29.jpg/170px-Aeroflot_flight_attendant_%28hostess%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Aeroflot_flight_attendant_%28hostess%29.jpg/255px-Aeroflot_flight_attendant_%28hostess%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Aeroflot_flight_attendant_%28hostess%29.jpg/340px-Aeroflot_flight_attendant_%28hostess%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aeroflot_flight_attendant_(hostess).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Aeroflot stewardess (2017)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rossiya,_EI-UNN,_Boeing_777-312_(32182478212).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1200" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Rossiya%2C_EI-UNN%2C_Boeing_777-312_%2832182478212%29.jpg/220px-Rossiya%2C_EI-UNN%2C_Boeing_777-312_%2832182478212%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Rossiya%2C_EI-UNN%2C_Boeing_777-312_%2832182478212%29.jpg/330px-Rossiya%2C_EI-UNN%2C_Boeing_777-312_%2832182478212%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Rossiya%2C_EI-UNN%2C_Boeing_777-312_%2832182478212%29.jpg/440px-Rossiya%2C_EI-UNN%2C_Boeing_777-312_%2832182478212%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rossiya,_EI-UNN,_Boeing_777-312_(32182478212).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rossiya_(airline)" title="Rossiya (airline)">
          Rossiya Airlines'
         </a>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boeing_777-300" title="Boeing 777-300">
          Boeing 777-300
         </a>
         in the new livery lands at
         <a href="/wiki/Pulkovo_Airport" title="Pulkovo Airport">
          Pulkovo Airport
         </a>
         in 2016. In November 2011
         <span style="display:none">
          (
          <span class="bday dtstart published updated">
           2011-11
          </span>
          )
         </span>
         , Aeroflot received 75% minus one share of Rossiya along with the shares of four other carriers.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Russia’s_Rossiya_Airlines_names_new_chairman_36-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-Russia’s_Rossiya_Airlines_names_new_chairman-36">
           [36]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In February 2010
       <span style="display:none">
        (
        <span class="bday dtstart published updated">
         2010-02
        </span>
        )
       </span>
       , the Russian government announced that all regional airlines owned by the state through the holding company
       <i>
        Rostechnologii
       </i>
       would be consolidated with the national carrier Aeroflot in order to increase the airlines' financial viability.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The merger was completed in late November 2011
       <span style="display:none">
        (
        <span class="bday dtstart published updated">
         2011-11
        </span>
        )
       </span>
       in a deal worth
       <span style="white-space: nowrap">
        <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">
         US$
        </a>
        81
       </span>
       million, Aeroflot's sister company
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Aeroflot-Finance&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Aeroflot-Finance (page does not exist)">
        Aeroflot-Finance
       </a>
       became the major shareholder of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vladivostok_Avia" title="Vladivostok Avia">
        Vladivostok Avia
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saravia" title="Saravia">
        Saravia
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Rossiya_Airlines" title="Rossiya Airlines">
        Rossiya Airlines
       </a>
       , and the sole shareholder of both
       <a href="/wiki/SAT_Airlines" title="SAT Airlines">
        SAT Airlines
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Orenair" title="Orenair">
        Orenair
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Russia’s_Rostechnology_finalizes_transfer_of_five_regional_carriers_to_Aeroflot_38-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Russia’s_Rostechnology_finalizes_transfer_of_five_regional_carriers_to_Aeroflot-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It was reported in January 2012
       <span style="display:none">
        (
        <span class="bday dtstart published updated">
         2012-01
        </span>
        )
       </span>
       that Saravia was sold to private investors, as the recent-acquired regional airline was not in line with Aeroflot's business strategy.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_sells_regional_subsidiary_39-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_sells_regional_subsidiary-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It was reported in June 2013
       <span style="display:none">
        (
        <span class="bday dtstart published updated">
         2013-06
        </span>
        )
       </span>
       that in the third quarter of the same year Aeroflot would combine its subsidiaries
       <a href="/wiki/Vladivostok_Air" title="Vladivostok Air">
        Vladivostok Air
       </a>
       and SAT Airlines into a new subsidiary regional carrier based in the
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Far_East" title="Russian Far East">
        Russian Far East
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_to_launch_Far_East_subsidiary_in_3Q_40-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_to_launch_Far_East_subsidiary_in_3Q-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The subsidiary was effectively created in September 2013
       <span style="display:none">
        (
        <span class="bday dtstart published updated">
         2013-09
