        </span>
        )
       </span>
       and was originally named
       <i>
        Taiga Airline
       </i>
       before later being renamed
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aurora_Airline" title="Aurora Airline">
         Aurora Airline
        </a>
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_provides_a_$13.5_million_loan_for_Far_East_subsidiary_41-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_provides_a_$13.5_million_loan_for_Far_East_subsidiary-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Russia’s_Aeroflot_creates_Far_East_subsidiary_Taiga_Airline_42-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Russia’s_Aeroflot_creates_Far_East_subsidiary_Taiga_Airline-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The new company, 51%-owned by Aeroflot, was expected to link Moscow with the Russian Far East, whereas SAT Airlines and Vladivostok Avia were expected to cease operations in early 2014.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_subsidiary_Aurora_Airline_set_to_launch_operations_43-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_subsidiary_Aurora_Airline_set_to_launch_operations-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In June 2013, during the World Airline Awards which took place at the 50th Le Bourget air show, Aeroflot was awarded the international prize as the best air carrier in Eastern Europe.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_recognized_as_best_air_carrier_in_Eastern_Europe_44-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_recognized_as_best_air_carrier_in_Eastern_Europe-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In October, the company introduced an affiliated
       <a href="/wiki/Low-cost_carrier" title="Low-cost carrier">
        low-cost carrier
       </a>
       (LCC),
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Dobrolet_(low-cost_airline)" title="Dobrolet (low-cost airline)">
         Dobrolet
        </a>
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_Introduces_New_Low-Cost_Airline_–_Dobrolet_45-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_Introduces_New_Low-Cost_Airline_–_Dobrolet-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aeroflot-introduces-new-low-cost-airline---dobrolet-133010_46-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-aeroflot-introduces-new-low-cost-airline---dobrolet-133010-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The LCC started operations in June 2014
       <span style="display:none">
        (
        <span class="bday dtstart published updated">
         2014-06
        </span>
        )
       </span>
       ;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_subsidiary_Dobrolet_launches_flights_47-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_subsidiary_Dobrolet_launches_flights-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       they ceased on 4 August 2014
       <span style="display:none">
        (
        <span class="dtend">
         2014-08-04
        </span>
        )
       </span>
       owing to EU sanctions over the airline launching flights to
       <a href="/wiki/Crimea" title="Crimea">
        Crimea
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Russia’s_Dobrolet_ceases_operations_due_to_EU_sanctions_48-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Russia’s_Dobrolet_ceases_operations_due_to_EU_sanctions-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dobrolet_halts_flights_as_EU_sanctions_block_jet_lease_49-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Dobrolet_halts_flights_as_EU_sanctions_block_jet_lease-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In late August 2014
       <span style="display:none">
        (
        <span class="bday dtstart published updated">
         2014-08
        </span>
        )
       </span>
       , Aeroflot announced the launch of a new LCC in October 2014
       <span style="display:none">
        (
        <span class="bday dtstart published updated">
         2014-10
        </span>
        )
       </span>
       to replace
       <i>
        Dobrolet
       </i>
       ; it would use aircraft transferred from Orenair.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_to_launch_new_LCC_subsidiary_50-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_to_launch_new_LCC_subsidiary-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The new LCC, named
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Pobeda_(airline)" title="Pobeda (airline)">
         Pobeda
        </a>
       </i>
       , started operations from Vnukovo Airport in December 2014
       <span style="display:none">
        (
        <span class="bday dtstart published updated">
         2014-12
        </span>
        )
       </span>
       ;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_acts_to_relaunch_its_LCC_project_with_Pobeda_after_Group_profits_fell_again_in_3Q2014_51-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_acts_to_relaunch_its_LCC_project_with_Pobeda_after_Group_profits_fell_again_in_3Q2014-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_subsidiary_Pobeda_launches_flights_52-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_subsidiary_Pobeda_launches_flights-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       it had plans to fly to
       <a href="/wiki/Belgorod" title="Belgorod">
        Belgorod
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kazan" title="Kazan">
        Kazan
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Perm" title="Perm">
        Perm
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Samara,_Russia" title="Samara, Russia">
        Samara
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Surgut" title="Surgut">
        Surgut
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tyumen" title="Tyumen">
        Tyumen
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ufa" title="Ufa">
        Ufa
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Volgograd" title="Volgograd">
        Volgograd
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Yekaterinburg" title="Yekaterinburg">
        Yekaterinburg
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_Aeroflot_budget_carrier_discloses_network_53-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-New_Aeroflot_budget_carrier_discloses_network-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In March 2014 as a response to
       <a href="/wiki/2014_Ukrainian_revolution" title="2014 Ukrainian revolution">
        2014 Ukrainian revolution
       </a>
       the company announced rerouting their flights to avoid flying over the territory of
       <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">
        Ukraine
       </a>
       . The announcement (together with worse than expected financial results) caused an almost 10% drop in the share price of the company.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
        <a href="#cite_note-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Also in March 2014
       <span style="display:none">
        (
        <span class="bday dtstart published updated">
         2014-03
        </span>
        )
       </span>
       , Aeroflot
       <span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">
        's
       </span>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IATA_airline_designator" title="IATA airline designator">
        flight designator
       </a>
       ″SU″ was adopted by its subsidiary Rossiya.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Russia’s_Rossiya_Airlines_names_new_chairman_36-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Russia’s_Rossiya_Airlines_names_new_chairman-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In September 2015, Aeroflot agreed to acquire 75% of
       <a href="/wiki/Transaero" title="Transaero">
        Transaero
       </a>
       Airlines for the symbolic price of one ruble,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
        <a href="#cite_note-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       but abandoned the plan later after failing to come to terms on a takeover.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
        <a href="#cite_note-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The carrier did take over a number of Transaero's aircraft by assuming its leases after the defunct airline's collapse. This introduced the
       <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747" title="Boeing 747">
        Boeing 747
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Boeing_777" title="Boeing 777">
        Boeing 777
       </a>
       to Aeroflot's fleet. In addition, the company suggested that it would cancel some of its jet orders as a result of the newly assumed aircraft.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
        <a href="#cite_note-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Following a prior announcement, Aeroflot
       <span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">
        's
       </span>
       subsidiaries Rossiya Airlines, Donavia and Orenair combined their operations in late March 2016
       <span style="display:none">
        (
        <span class="bday dtstart published updated">
         2016-03
        </span>
        )
       </span>
       . Orenair
       <span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">
        's
       </span>
       AOC was cancelled by Russian authorities in late May 2016
       <span style="display:none">
        (
        <span class="dtend">
         2016-05
        </span>
        )
       </span>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_files_for_bankruptcy_of_Orenair,_Donavia_subsidiaries_59-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_files_for_bankruptcy_of_Orenair,_Donavia_subsidiaries-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Russian_authorities_cancel_Orenair’s_AOC_60-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Russian_authorities_cancel_Orenair’s_AOC-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Aeroflot filed both Donavia and Orenair for bankruptcy in January 2017.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_files_for_bankruptcy_of_Orenair,_Donavia_subsidiaries_59-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_files_for_bankruptcy_of_Orenair,_Donavia_subsidiaries-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Orenair and Donavia were formally declared bankrupt in February 2017 and August 2017, respectively.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Russian_court_declares_Aeroflot_subsidiary_Donavia_bankrupt_61-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Russian_court_declares_Aeroflot_subsidiary_Donavia_bankrupt-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_affairs">
        Corporate affairs
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">

        </span>

        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Headquarters">
        Headquarters
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Aeroflot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Headquarters">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Moscow,_Arbat_12-10.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="992" data-file-width="800" height="211" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Moscow%2C_Arbat_12-10.JPG/170px-Moscow%2C_Arbat_12-10.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Moscow%2C_Arbat_12-10.JPG/255px-Moscow%2C_Arbat_12-10.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Moscow%2C_Arbat_12-10.JPG/340px-Moscow%2C_Arbat_12-10.JPG 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Moscow,_Arbat_12-10.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Aeroflot headquarters are in the light yellow building, 10 Arbat Street, Moscow
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The headquarters of Aeroflot are located in
       <a href="/wiki/Arbat_District" title="Arbat District">
        Arbat District
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Administrative_Okrug" title="Central Administrative Okrug">
        Central Administrative Okrug
       </a>
       , Moscow.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
        <a href="#cite_note-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By 2009 Aeroflot began leasing 7,000 square metres (75,000 sq ft) of space from a class A office building on
       <a href="/wiki/Arbat_Street" title="Arbat Street">
        Arbat Street
       </a>
       owned by Midland Development. As of that year Aeroflot had plans to build a dedicated 35,000 square metres (380,000 sq ft) headquarters in proximity to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sheremetyevo_Airport" title="Sheremetyevo Airport">
        Sheremetyevo Airport
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Key_people">
        Key people
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Aeroflot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Key people">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       As of December 2014
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Aeroflot&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , Aeroflot's CEO position is held by
       <a href="/wiki/Vitaly_Savelyev" title="Vitaly Savelyev">
        Vitaly Savelyev
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_acts_to_relaunch_its_LCC_project_with_Pobeda_after_Group_profits_fell_again_in_3Q2014_51-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_acts_to_relaunch_its_LCC_project_with_Pobeda_after_Group_profits_fell_again_in_3Q2014-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Savelyev was appointed on 10 April 2009
       <span style="display:none">
        (
        <span class="bday dtstart published updated">
         2009-04-10
        </span>
        )
       </span>
       and succeeded Valery Okulov. Expiring in April 2014
       <span style="display:none">
        (
        <span class="dtend">
         2014-04
        </span>
        )
       </span>
       , The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_government" title="Russian government">
        Russian government
       </a>
       extended Savelyev's appointment for another five years.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Saveliev_to_lead_Aeroflot_for_next_five_years_64-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Saveliev_to_lead_Aeroflot_for_next_five_years-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ownership_and_subsidiaries">
        Ownership and subsidiaries
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Aeroflot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Ownership and subsidiaries">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       As of December 2013
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Aeroflot&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , Aeroflot was 51% state-owned.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
        <a href="#cite_note-65">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Aeroflot Group, Russia’s largest airline
       <a href="/wiki/Holding_company" title="Holding company">
        holding company
       </a>
       , includes several subsidiaries:
       <a href="/wiki/Pobeda_(airline)" title="Pobeda (airline)">
        Pobeda
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Rossiya_Airlines" title="Rossiya Airlines">
        Rossiya
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Donavia" title="Donavia">
        Donavia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Orenair" title="Orenair">
        Orenair
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Aurora_(airline)" title="Aurora (airline)">
        Aurora
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AeroflotProfile_66-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-AeroflotProfile-66">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
       At that time, the Aeroflot Group employed 30,328; 17,678 of these people worked for Aeroflot JSC.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot:_strong_profit_growth_in_9M2013._LCC_subsidiary_Dobrolet_complements_the_team_in_early_2014_67-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot:_strong_profit_growth_in_9M2013._LCC_subsidiary_Dobrolet_complements_the_team_in_early_2014-67">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Staffing">
        Staffing
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Aeroflot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Staffing">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In 2016 the company decided to link the pay of its flight attendants to their dress size. All the flight attendants were photographed, measured and some were weighed. Women above a Russian size 48 were barred from international flights.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
        <a href="#cite_note-68">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
       According to the flight attendants’ trade union the policy affected about 600 Aeroflot attendants. The company successfully defended itself in court in April 2017 by saying that a survey of Aeroflot passengers showed that “92% want to see stewardesses who fit into the clothes sizes we are talking about here”
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
        <a href="#cite_note-69">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and that every extra kilogramme meant spending an extra 800 roubles per year on fuel.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
        <a href="#cite_note-70">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The company denied all the accusations of discrimination.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
        <a href="#cite_note-71">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In September 2017 the appeal court decided that requirements banning employment by women who wore large sizes was unenforceable and ordered compensation for Yevgenia Magurina, a flight attendant who filed a discrimination suit.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
        <a href="#cite_note-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Two women were awarded token compensation, but the court did not rule explicitly that the policy was discriminatory.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
        <a href="#cite_note-73">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Destinations">
        Destinations
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Aeroflot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Destinations">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Aeroflot_destinations" title="Aeroflot destinations">
        Aeroflot destinations
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       As of December 2013
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Aeroflot&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , Aeroflot operates scheduled passenger and cargo flights from its hub at
       <a href="/wiki/Sheremetyevo_International_Airport" title="Sheremetyevo International Airport">
        Sheremetyevo International Airport
       </a>
       to 129 airports.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
        <a href="#cite_note-74">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Fleet">
        Fleet
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Aeroflot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Fleet">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History_and_recent_developments">
        History and recent developments
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Aeroflot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: History and recent developments">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       During the Soviet era, almost all Aeroflot's airliners were built by Soviet manufacturers. During the 1940s and the early 1950s, the main aircraft was the
       <a href="/wiki/Lisunov_Li-2" title="Lisunov Li-2">
        Lisunov Li-2
       </a>
       a license-built version of the
       <a href="/wiki/Douglas_DC-3" title="Douglas DC-3">
        Douglas DC-3
       </a>
       . The first to be produced in the Soviet Union was completed in 1939. DC-3s modified by fitting Soviet-made engines, named the PS-84, were also used later. The Li-2 would be replaced by the
       <a href="/wiki/Ilyushin_Il-12" title="Ilyushin Il-12">
        Ilyushin Il-12
       </a>
       , which entered service in 1947, and the
       <a href="/wiki/Ilyushin_Il-14" title="Ilyushin Il-14">
        Ilyushin Il-14
       </a>
       , which entered service in 1954. Aeroflot also operated thousands of the
       <a href="/wiki/Antonov_An-2" title="Antonov An-2">
        Antonov An-2
       </a>
       STOL biplane (first flying in 1947), in passenger and cargo roles. The An-2 remained in service until the 1980s.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aeroflot_Tu-104B_CCCP-42403_LBG_1974-8-2.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="855" data-file-width="1279" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Aeroflot_Tu-104B_CCCP-42403_LBG_1974-8-2.png/220px-Aeroflot_Tu-104B_CCCP-42403_LBG_1974-8-2.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Aeroflot_Tu-104B_CCCP-42403_LBG_1974-8-2.png/330px-Aeroflot_Tu-104B_CCCP-42403_LBG_1974-8-2.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Aeroflot_Tu-104B_CCCP-42403_LBG_1974-8-2.png/440px-Aeroflot_Tu-104B_CCCP-42403_LBG_1974-8-2.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aeroflot_Tu-104B_CCCP-42403_LBG_1974-8-2.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         An Aeroflot
         <a href="/wiki/Tupolev_Tu-104" title="Tupolev Tu-104">
          Tupolev Tu-104
         </a>
         at
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Le_Bourget_Airport" title="Le Bourget Airport">
          Le Bourget Airport
         </a>
         in 1974.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Aeroflot began operating the
       <a href="/wiki/Tupolev_Tu-104" title="Tupolev Tu-104">
        Tupolev Tu-104
       </a>
       , reportedly named
       <i>
        Silver Arrow
       </i>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Flight1956-659_76-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Flight1956-659-76">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
       with at least three of these machines in service between Moscow and the
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Far_East" title="Russian Far East">
        Russian Far East
       </a>
       by June 1956
       <span style="display:none">
        (
        <span class="bday dtstart published updated">
         1956-06
        </span>
        )
       </span>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Flight1956-854_77-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Flight1956-854-77">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Tu-104 was the USSR's first
       <a href="/wiki/Jet_aircraft" title="Jet aircraft">
        jet airliner
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Flight1959-615_78-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Flight1959-615-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         615
        </span>
       </sup>
       The first two routes on which it was deployed were the Moscow–
       <a href="/wiki/Irkutsk" title="Irkutsk">
        Irkutsk
       </a>
       and the Moscow–
       <a href="/wiki/Yakutsk" title="Yakutsk">
        Yakutsk
       </a>
       runs;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Flight1956-659_76-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Flight1956-659-76">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
        <a href="#cite_note-79">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
       in September 1956
       <span style="display:none">
        (
        <span class="bday dtstart published updated">
         1956-09
        </span>
        )
       </span>
       , the Moscow–
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tiflis" title="Tiflis">
        Tiflis
       </a>
       route became the third scheduled service flown with the aircraft.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Flight1956-596_80-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Flight1956-596-80">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Likewise, Moscow–
       <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">
        Prague
       </a>
       was the first international route served with the Silver Arrow.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Flight1956-659_76-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Flight1956-659-76">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1962, Aeroflot began operating the
       <a href="/wiki/Tupolev_Tu-124" title="Tupolev Tu-124">
        Tupolev Tu-124
       </a>
       , the smaller version of the Tu-104, on regional routes. These were later replaced by the
       <a href="/wiki/Tupolev_Tu-134" title="Tupolev Tu-134">
        Tupolev Tu-134
       </a>
       , which entered service in 1967. The
       <a href="/wiki/Tupolev_Tu-114" title="Tupolev Tu-114">
        Tupolev Tu-114
       </a>
       , originally used to transport Soviet leaders and once the world
       <span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">
        's
       </span>
       largest commercial aircraft, came into service on 24 April 1961
       <span style="display:none">
        (
        <span class="bday dtstart published updated">
         1961-04-24
        </span>
        )
       </span>
       on the Moscow–
       <a href="/wiki/Khabarovsk" title="Khabarovsk">
        Khabarovsk
       </a>
       route.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FI1964-936_81-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FI1964-936-81">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FI1964-492_82-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FI1964-492-82">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It also served international routes, such as Moscow–Tokyo in conjunction with
       <a href="/wiki/Japan_Airlines" title="Japan Airlines">
        Japan Airlines
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JAL_Expands_83-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-JAL_Expands-83">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
       as well as the Moscow–
       <a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">
        Havana
       </a>
       route, which started on 7 January 1963
       <span style="display:none">
        (
        <span class="bday dtstart published updated">
         1963-01-07
        </span>
        )
       </span>
       —the airline's longest non-stop service at that time.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FI1964-492_82-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FI1964-492-82">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tu-114_Moscow—Havana_84-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Tu-114_Moscow—Havana-84">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The first
       <a href="/wiki/Ilyushin_Il-62" title="Ilyushin Il-62">
        Ilyushin Il-62
       </a>
       long-range four-engined airliner entered service with Aeroflot in 1967, with an inaugural flight from Moscow to
       <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">
        Montreal
       </a>
       on 15 September.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
        <a href="#cite_note-85">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It was complemented, in 1972, by medium-range
       <a href="/wiki/Tupolev_Tu-154" title="Tupolev Tu-154">
        Tupolev Tu-154
       </a>
       . This jet is the most popular Russian airliner, with more than 1,000 made. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tu-154M" title="Tu-154M">
        Tu-154M
       </a>
       variant was delivered to Aeroflot in 1984.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Commercial_Aircraft_Directory:_Part_2_86-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Commercial_Aircraft_Directory:_Part_2-86">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aeroflot_Il-86_CCCP-86080_FCO_Feb_1992.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="799" data-file-width="1199" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Aeroflot_Il-86_CCCP-86080_FCO_Feb_1992.png/220px-Aeroflot_Il-86_CCCP-86080_FCO_Feb_1992.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Aeroflot_Il-86_CCCP-86080_FCO_Feb_1992.png/330px-Aeroflot_Il-86_CCCP-86080_FCO_Feb_1992.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Aeroflot_Il-86_CCCP-86080_FCO_Feb_1992.png/440px-Aeroflot_Il-86_CCCP-86080_FCO_Feb_1992.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aeroflot_Il-86_CCCP-86080_FCO_Feb_1992.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         An Aeroflot
         <a href="/wiki/Ilyushin_Il-86" title="Ilyushin Il-86">
          Ilyushin Il-86
         </a>
         at
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fiumicino_Airport" title="Fiumicino Airport">
          Fiumicino Airport
         </a>
         in 1992.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tupolev_TU-144_(6060104119).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2266" data-file-width="3435" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Tupolev_TU-144_%286060104119%29.jpg/220px-Tupolev_TU-144_%286060104119%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Tupolev_TU-144_%286060104119%29.jpg/330px-Tupolev_TU-144_%286060104119%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Tupolev_TU-144_%286060104119%29.jpg/440px-Tupolev_TU-144_%286060104119%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tupolev_TU-144_(6060104119).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         An Aeroflot
         <a href="/wiki/Tupolev_Tu-144" title="Tupolev Tu-144">
          Tupolev Tu-144
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The carrier started flying the supersonic
       <a href="/wiki/Tupolev_Tu-144" title="Tupolev Tu-144">
        Tupolev Tu-144
       </a>
       on freighter services in 1975.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FI1976-1693_87-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FI1976-1693-87">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On 1 November 1977
       <span style="display:none">
        (
        <span class="bday dtstart published updated">
         1977-11-01
        </span>
        )
       </span>
       , the aircraft was deployed on the 1,750-nautical-mile (3,240 km; 2,010 mi) long
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Domodedovo_International_Airport" title="Domodedovo International Airport">
        Moscow-Domodedovo
       </a>
       –
       <a href="/wiki/Almaty" title="Almaty">
        Alma-Ata
       </a>
       route on a regular basis,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tu-144_enters_passenger_service_88-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Tu-144_enters_passenger_service-88">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
       yet these services were discontinued in May 1978
       <span style="display:none">
        (
        <span class="bday dtstart published updated">
         1978-05
        </span>
        )
       </span>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Supersonic_resurrection_89-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Supersonic_resurrection-89">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
       That month, an aircraft of the type resulted
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Written_off" title="Written off">
        written off
       </a>
       on an emergency landing following an electrical failure, withdrawing political support to the project and putting an end to the production.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-History_90-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-History-90">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Despite official versions indicating the indefinite suspension of supersonic flights within the Soviet Union, a re-engined version of the aircraft was put on a test flight between Moscow and Khabarovsk in June 1979
       <span style="display:none">
        (
        <span class="bday dtstart published updated">
         1979-06
        </span>
        )
       </span>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tu-144_flies_again_91-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Tu-144_flies_again-91">
         [91]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the 3,750-mile (6,040 km) long route was later covered with scheduled services;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_Tu-144_engines_reported_92-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-New_Tu-144_engines_reported-92">
         [92]
        </a>
       </sup>
       it was not a nonstop flight, however, since the aircraft had to make a refuelling stop, as the engines consumed more fuel than expected.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-History_90-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-History-90">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
       First flown in March 1975
       <span style="display:none">
        (
        <span class="bday dtstart published updated">
         1975-03
        </span>
        )
       </span>
       , the 120-seater
       <a href="/wiki/Yakovlev_Yak-42" title="Yakovlev Yak-42">
        Yakovlev Yak-42
       </a>
       entered service with Aeroflot in 1980.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Commercial_Aircraft_Directory:_Part_2_86-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Commercial_Aircraft_Directory:_Part_2-86">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The 350-seater
       <a href="/wiki/Ilyushin_Il-86" title="Ilyushin Il-86">
        Ilyushin Il-86
       </a>
       , the first Russian-made
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wide-body" title="Wide-body">
        wide-body
       </a>
       aircraft,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FI1982-1214/1215_93-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FI1982-1214/1215-93">
         [93]
        </a>
       </sup>
       had its
       <a href="/wiki/Maiden_flight" title="Maiden flight">
        maiden flight
       </a>
       in December 1976
       <span style="display:none">
        (
        <span class="bday dtstart published updated">
         1976-12
        </span>
        )
       </span>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Commercial_Aircraft_Directory:_Part_2_86-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Commercial_Aircraft_Directory:_Part_2-86">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FI1985-62_94-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FI1985-62-94">
         [94]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and entered scheduled services with the carrier on the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moscow-Vnukovo" title="Moscow-Vnukovo">
        Moscow-Vnukovo
       </a>
       –
       <a href="/wiki/Tashkent" title="Tashkent">
        Tashkent
       </a>
       run in 1981.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FI1981-206_95-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FI1981-206-95">
         [95]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
        <a href="#cite_note-97">
         [nb 1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The aircraft was phased out by the end of 2006.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_fleet_renewal_continues_with_end_of_IL-86s,_lease_of_A321s_98-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_fleet_renewal_continues_with_end_of_IL-86s,_lease_of_A321s-98">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aeroflot_Boeing_767-300ER_VP-BAZ_SVO_2001-4-1.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="550" data-file-width="826" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Aeroflot_Boeing_767-300ER_VP-BAZ_SVO_2001-4-1.png/220px-Aeroflot_Boeing_767-300ER_VP-BAZ_SVO_2001-4-1.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Aeroflot_Boeing_767-300ER_VP-BAZ_SVO_2001-4-1.png/330px-Aeroflot_Boeing_767-300ER_VP-BAZ_SVO_2001-4-1.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Aeroflot_Boeing_767-300ER_VP-BAZ_SVO_2001-4-1.png/440px-Aeroflot_Boeing_767-300ER_VP-BAZ_SVO_2001-4-1.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aeroflot_Boeing_767-300ER_VP-BAZ_SVO_2001-4-1.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         An Aeroflot
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boeing_767-300ER" title="Boeing 767-300ER">
          Boeing 767-300ER
         </a>
         in old livery on short final to
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sheremetyevo_Airport" title="Sheremetyevo Airport">
          Sheremetyevo Airport
         </a>
         in 2001.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The first Western-made aircraft, the
       <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A310" title="Airbus A310">
        Airbus A310
       </a>
       , was incorporated into the fleet in 1992. This milestone also made Aeroflot the first Russian customer for
       <a href="/wiki/Airbus" title="Airbus">
        Airbus
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_takes_delivery_of_first_sharklet-equipped_A320_99-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_takes_delivery_of_first_sharklet-equipped_A320-99">
         [98]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_to_acquire_22_A350XWBs_and_10_A330s_100-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_to_acquire_22_A350XWBs_and_10_A330s-100">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The first example of the
       <a href="/wiki/Ilyushin_Il-96" title="Ilyushin Il-96">
        Ilyushin Il-96
       </a>
       , which was also the first Soviet
       <a href="/wiki/Fly-by-wire" title="Fly-by-wire">
        fly-by-wire
       </a>
       aircraft, had its maiden flight in 1988, and was certificated in December 1992
       <span style="display:none">
        (
        <span class="bday dtstart published updated">
         1992-12
        </span>
        )
       </span>
       ;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ilyushin_96-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ilyushin-96">
         [96]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the first Aeroflot Il-96-300 entered the fleet in 1993,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FI1993-18_101-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FI1993-18-101">
         [100]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and was initially deployed on the Moscow–New York City route in July that year.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FI1994-49/50_102-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FI1994-49/50-102">
         [101]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         50
        </span>
       </sup>
       Pending approval for an
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ex-Im_Bank" title="Ex-Im Bank">
        Ex-Im Bank
       </a>
       financing package, a contract worth
       <span style="white-space: nowrap">
        <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">
         US$
        </a>
        1.5
       </span>
       billion for the acquisition of twenty Il-96s, including ten Il-96T cargo aircraft and ten Il-96Ms that were initially slated for delivery between 1996 and 1999, was signed in June 1995
       <span style="display:none">
        (
        <span class="bday dtstart published updated">
         1995-06
        </span>
        )
       </span>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ARIA_Il-96_order_in_the_balance_103-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ARIA_Il-96_order_in_the_balance-103">
         [102]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Ex-Im Bank approved the loan in early 1996.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Exim_approves_Aeroflot_financing_104-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Exim_approves_Aeroflot_financing-104">
         [103]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Boeing" title="Boeing">
        Boeing
       </a>
       objected to the deal, but the dispute was later settled following an Aeroflot order for ten
       <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_Classic" title="Boeing 737 Classic">
        Boeing 737-400s
       </a>
       —placed in April 1997
       <span style="display:none">
        (
        <span class="bday dtstart published updated">
         1997-04
        </span>
        )
       </span>
       in a deal worth
       <span style="white-space: nowrap">
        US$440
       </span>
       million
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_Orders_Ten_Boeing_737-400_Twinjets_105-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_Orders_Ten_Boeing_737-400_Twinjets-105">
         [104]
        </a>
       </sup>
       — that were granted a
       <a href="/wiki/Tax_exemption" title="Tax exemption">
        tax exemption
       </a>
       by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_government" title="Russian government">
        Russian government
       </a>
       ; nevertheless, the financing was blocked again when four
       <a href="/wiki/Boeing_767" title="Boeing 767">
        Boeing 767-300ERs
       </a>
       also ordered by Aeroflot were not included in the accorded exemption.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USA/Russia_argue_over_Il-96_Exim_Bank_deal_106-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-USA/Russia_argue_over_Il-96_Exim_Bank_deal-106">
         [105]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Later on these four aircraft were also exempted from paying customs taxes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Customs_waiver_clears_Aeroflot_767-300ER_lease_deal_107-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Customs_waiver_clears_Aeroflot_767-300ER_lease_deal-107">
         [106]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The first of these Boeing 767-300ERs commenced operating in August 1999
       <span style="display:none">
        (
        <span class="bday dtstart published updated">
         1999-08
        </span>
        )
       </span>
       ;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Milestone_Boeing_767-300ER_Delivered_to_Aeroflot_--_Russian_International_Airlines_108-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Milestone_Boeing_767-300ER_Delivered_to_Aeroflot_--_Russian_International_Airlines-108">
         [107]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the airline had taken delivery of the first Boeing 737–400 in May the same year.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_Takes_Delivery_of_its_First_Boeing_737-400_109-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_Takes_Delivery_of_its_First_Boeing_737-400-109">
         [108]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       From 1998 to 2005, Aeroflot leased two
       <a href="/wiki/Boeing_777" title="Boeing 777">
        Boeing 777s
       </a>
       , using the type on routes to the USA.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">
        <a href="#cite_note-110">
         [109]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Matters came to a head in September 2006 as Aeroflot's board of directors convened to vote on the Boeing contract. This coincided with the USA imposing sanctions on various Russian companies (including a major aircraft maker,
       <a href="/wiki/Sukhoi" title="Sukhoi">
        Sukhoi
       </a>
       ) for allegedly supplying Iran in violation of the US's
       <a href="/wiki/Iran_Nonproliferation_Act_of_2000" title="Iran Nonproliferation Act of 2000">
        Iran Nonproliferation Act of 2000
       </a>
       and with the Russian state-owned
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vneshtorgbank" title="Vneshtorgbank">
        Vneshtorgbank
       </a>
       buying 5% of the stock in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EADS" title="EADS">
        EADS
       </a>
       , the corporation behind Airbus. The State's representatives on the board abstained from the vote and another round of lobbying ensued, with Russian news sources reporting Aeroflot's efforts to placate the State by offering to order both 22 Boeing 787s
       <i>
        and
       </i>
       22 Airbus 350s, effectively doubling its long-range fleet.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_to_buy_22_Boeing_planes,_22_from_Airbus_111-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_to_buy_22_Boeing_planes,_22_from_Airbus-111">
         [110]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Banker
       <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Lebedev" title="Alexander Lebedev">
        Alexander Lebedev
       </a>
       , the man behind National Reserve Corporation, reached a deal with Boeing to prolong the deadline, using his corporation's money.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_reserves_22_Boeing_jets_112-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_reserves_22_Boeing_jets-112">
         [111]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aeroflot_Airbus_A330_Kustov.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3000" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Aeroflot_Airbus_A330_Kustov.jpg/220px-Aeroflot_Airbus_A330_Kustov.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Aeroflot_Airbus_A330_Kustov.jpg/330px-Aeroflot_Airbus_A330_Kustov.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Aeroflot_Airbus_A330_Kustov.jpg/440px-Aeroflot_Airbus_A330_Kustov.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aeroflot_Airbus_A330_Kustov.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         An
         <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A330" title="Airbus A330">
          Airbus A330-200
         </a>
         just departed from Sheremetyevo Airport in 2011.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In March 2007
       <span style="display:none">
        (
        <span class="bday dtstart published updated">
         2007-03
        </span>
        )
       </span>
       , Aeroflot signed a
       <a href="/wiki/Memorandum_of_understanding" title="Memorandum of understanding">
        memorandum of understanding
       </a>
       with Airbus for the acquisition of 22
       <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A350_XWB" title="Airbus A350 XWB">
        Airbus A350 XWBs
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boeing,_Aeroflot_sign_'Dreamliner'_deal_113-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Boeing,_Aeroflot_sign_'Dreamliner'_deal-113">
         [112]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and 10
       <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A330" title="Airbus A330">
        Airbus A330-200s
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_to_acquire_22_A350XWBs_and_10_A330s_100-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_to_acquire_22_A350XWBs_and_10_A330s-100">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_modernizing_with_A350_XWB_commitment,_e-ticketing_114-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_modernizing_with_A350_XWB_commitment,_e-ticketing-114">
         [113]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The transaction for the A350 XWBs was formalised late that year in a deal worth
       <span style="white-space: nowrap">
        US$3.1
       </span>
       billion.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Price_of_Aeroflot_Airbus_Purchase_Revealed_as_$3.1Bln_115-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Price_of_Aeroflot_Airbus_Purchase_Revealed_as_$3.1Bln-115">
         [114]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The handover of the first A350 XWB was due to take place in 2015. Delivery has been delayed by three years, with the first aircraft to enter the fleet in 2018.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_to_delay_A350_XWB_deliveries_116-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_to_delay_A350_XWB_deliveries-116">
         [115]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A contract for the acquisition of 22
       <a href="/wiki/Boeing_787_Dreamliner" title="Boeing 787 Dreamliner">
        Boeing 787 Dreamliners
       </a>
       was signed in June 2007
       <span style="display:none">
        (
        <span class="bday dtstart published updated">
         2007-06
        </span>
        )
       </span>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Russia's_Aeroflot_signs_for_22_Boeing_787s_117-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Russia's_Aeroflot_signs_for_22_Boeing_787s-117">
         [116]
        </a>
       </sup>
       reportedly consisting of Boeing 787-8s with deliveries starting in 2014;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_787_order_part_of_deepening_Boeing-Russia_ties_118-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_787_order_part_of_deepening_Boeing-Russia_ties-118">
         [117]
        </a>
       </sup>
       in September the same year, Boeing officially announced that Aeroflot placed an order for these aircraft in a deal worth
       <span style="white-space: nowrap">
        <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">
         US$
        </a>
        3.6
       </span>
       billion.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boeing,_Aeroflot_Finalize_Order_for_22_787_Dreamliners_119-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Boeing,_Aeroflot_Finalize_Order_for_22_787_Dreamliners-119">
         [118]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Airbus A330 order was split into five A330-200s and five A330-300s, scheduled to arrive on an operating lease starting in late 2008. The first Airbus A330 entered the fleet in late 2008; it was an A330-200 and was initially put into service on the Moscow–St. Petersburg route for testing purposes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PICTURE:_Aeroflot_tests_first_A330_on_local_route_ahead_of_Asia_entry_120-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-PICTURE:_Aeroflot_tests_first_A330_on_local_route_ahead_of_Asia_entry-120">
         [119]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Despite the A330s having been initially aimed at providing interim capacity ahead of the arrival of both the Airbus A350s and the Boeing 787s the company had previously ordered, the type has been gradually incorporated into the fleet on a long-term basis. During the
       <a href="/wiki/Paris_Air_Show" title="Paris Air Show">
        2015 Paris Air Show
       </a>
       , Aeroflot cancelled the Dreamliner order.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PARIS:_Aeroflot_cancels_787_order_121-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-PARIS:_Aeroflot_cancels_787_order-121">
         [120]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aeroflot_Sukhoi_Superjet_100-95_RA-89002_SVO_2012-4-6.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1065" data-file-width="1599" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Aeroflot_Sukhoi_Superjet_100-95_RA-89002_SVO_2012-4-6.png/220px-Aeroflot_Sukhoi_Superjet_100-95_RA-89002_SVO_2012-4-6.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Aeroflot_Sukhoi_Superjet_100-95_RA-89002_SVO_2012-4-6.png/330px-Aeroflot_Sukhoi_Superjet_100-95_RA-89002_SVO_2012-4-6.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Aeroflot_Sukhoi_Superjet_100-95_RA-89002_SVO_2012-4-6.png/440px-Aeroflot_Sukhoi_Superjet_100-95_RA-89002_SVO_2012-4-6.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aeroflot_Sukhoi_Superjet_100-95_RA-89002_SVO_2012-4-6.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         An Aeroflot
         <a href="/wiki/Sukhoi_Superjet_100" title="Sukhoi Superjet 100">
          Sukhoi Superjet 100
         </a>
         at Sheremetyevo Airport in 2013.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In May 2007
       <span style="display:none">
        (
        <span class="bday dtstart published updated">
         2007-05
        </span>
        )
       </span>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Finnair" title="Finnair">
        Finnair
       </a>
       announced the sale of its last two self-owned
       <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_MD-11" title="McDonnell Douglas MD-11">
        McDonnell Douglas MD-11s
       </a>
       to Aeroflot which became part of the Russian airline's cargo fleet in 2008 and 2009.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Finnair_sells_two_Boeing_MD-11_aircraft_122-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Finnair_sells_two_Boeing_MD-11_aircraft-122">
         [121]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On 31 December 2007, Aeroflot retired the last
       <a href="/wiki/Tupolev_Tu-134" title="Tupolev Tu-134">
        Tupolev Tu-134
       </a>
       after 40 years in service;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Other_News_–_02/16/2007_123-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Other_News_–_02/16/2007-123">
         [122]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the last flight flew the
       <a href="/wiki/Kaliningrad" title="Kaliningrad">
        Kaliningrad
       </a>
       –Moscow route.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Other_News_–_01/03/2008_124-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Other_News_–_01/03/2008-124">
         [123]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Aeroflot was forced to withdraw these aircraft from service due to noise restrictions. Fourteen Tu-134s comprised the type's fleet by that time; they were offered for sale to the sister companies.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_ends_mainline_Tu-134_operations_after_40_years_125-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_ends_mainline_Tu-134_operations_after_40_years-125">
         [124]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The retirement of the last
       <a href="/wiki/Tupolev_Tu-154" title="Tupolev Tu-154">
        Tupolev Tu-154
       </a>
       occurred on 14 January 2010, after 40 years of service; the last flight the type operated was
       <a href="/wiki/Yekaterinburg" title="Yekaterinburg">
        Yekaterinburg
       </a>
       –Moscow, taking place on 31 December 2009.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Other_News_–_01/14/2010_126-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Other_News_–_01/14/2010-126">
         [125]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aeroflot_Boeing_777-300ER_VP-BGC_SVO_2013-3-7.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="683" data-file-width="1024" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Aeroflot_Boeing_777-300ER_VP-BGC_SVO_2013-3-7.png/220px-Aeroflot_Boeing_777-300ER_VP-BGC_SVO_2013-3-7.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Aeroflot_Boeing_777-300ER_VP-BGC_SVO_2013-3-7.png/330px-Aeroflot_Boeing_777-300ER_VP-BGC_SVO_2013-3-7.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Aeroflot_Boeing_777-300ER_VP-BGC_SVO_2013-3-7.png/440px-Aeroflot_Boeing_777-300ER_VP-BGC_SVO_2013-3-7.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aeroflot_Boeing_777-300ER_VP-BGC_SVO_2013-3-7.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         An Aeroflot
         <a href="/wiki/Boeing_777" title="Boeing 777">
          Boeing 777-300ER
         </a>
         lands at
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sheremetyevo_Airport" title="Sheremetyevo Airport">
          Sheremetyevo Airport
         </a>
         in 2013. The type was first ordered in 2011.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_board_approves_last_777_sale-and-leasebacks_127-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_board_approves_last_777_sale-and-leasebacks-127">
           [126]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In July 2010
       <span style="display:none">
        (
        <span class="bday dtstart published updated">
         2010-07
        </span>
        )
       </span>
       , Aeroflot announced a new A330 order during the
       <a href="/wiki/Farnborough_Airshow" title="Farnborough Airshow">
        Farnborough Airshow
       </a>
       , this time for 11 A330-300s.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FARNBOROUGH:_Aeroflot_firms_A330-300_order_128-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FARNBOROUGH:_Aeroflot_firms_A330-300_order-128">
         [127]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Also in July 2010
       <span style="display:none">
        (
        <span class="bday dtstart published updated">
         2010-07
        </span>
        )
       </span>
       , Russian prime minister
       <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">
        Vladimir Putin
       </a>
       pressured Aeroflot to
       <a href="/wiki/Protectionism" title="Protectionism">
        buy Russian-made aircraft
       </a>
       for future expansion and fleet renewal.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_plans_up_to_50_MS-21s_as_part_of_effort_to_support_Russia’s_airliner_industry_129-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_plans_up_to_50_MS-21s_as_part_of_effort_to_support_Russia’s_airliner_industry-129">
         [128]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Putin_pressures_Aeroflot_to_take_Russian-built_aircraft_130-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Putin_pressures_Aeroflot_to_take_Russian-built_aircraft-130">
         [129]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On 1 September 2010, Aeroflot announced that it had plans to order a total of 126 Russian-built aircraft by 2020. The aircraft to be purchased are
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irkut_MS-21" title="Irkut MS-21">
        Irkut MS-21s
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sukhoi_Superjet_100" title="Sukhoi Superjet 100">
        Sukhoi Superjet 100s
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Antonov_An-140" title="Antonov An-140">
        Antonov An-140s
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Antonov_An-148" title="Antonov An-148">
        Antonov An-148s
       </a>
       . The aircraft are to be used for fleet replacement in Aeroflot, as well as six other airlines of which Aeroflot is taking control.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_plans_up_to_50_MS-21s_as_part_of_effort_to_support_Russia’s_airliner_industry_129-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_plans_up_to_50_MS-21s_as_part_of_effort_to_support_Russia’s_airliner_industry-129">
         [128]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In February 2011
       <span style="display:none">
        (
        <span class="bday dtstart published updated">
         2011-02
        </span>
        )
       </span>
       , the carrier ordered eight Boeing 777-300ERs;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_board_approves_last_777_sale-and-leasebacks_127-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_board_approves_last_777_sale-and-leasebacks-127">
         [126]
        </a>
       </sup>
       later that year the order was boosted to sixteen aircraft.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boeing_orders_keep_coming_in_Paris_131-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Boeing_orders_keep_coming_in_Paris-131">
         [130]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Aeroflot became the second worldwide operator of the Sukhoi Superjet 100 when
       <a href="/wiki/Sukhoi" title="Sukhoi">
        Sukhoi
       </a>
       delivered the first aircraft of the type to the company in June 2011
       <span style="display:none">
        (
        <span class="bday dtstart published updated">
         2011-06
        </span>
        )
       </span>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_takes_delivery_of_first_Superjet_100_132-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_takes_delivery_of_first_Superjet_100-132">
         [131]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The first Boeing 777-300ER was handed over to the airline on 30 January 2013. Following delivery, it was planned to deploy the aircraft on the Moscow–Bangkok route, yet certification issues postponed these plans for days,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Missing_certificate_causes_Aeroflot_to_postpone_Boeing_777_operations_133-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Missing_certificate_causes_Aeroflot_to_postpone_Boeing_777_operations-133">
         [132]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_Boeing_777-300ER_Grounded_by_Missing_Certificate_134-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_Boeing_777-300ER_Grounded_by_Missing_Certificate-134">
         [133]
        </a>
       </sup>
       as permission to operate the aircraft was granted a few days later.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_receives_certificate_to_operate_Boeing_777_135-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_receives_certificate_to_operate_Boeing_777-135">
         [134]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In addition to the current firm contract for 30 Sukhoi Superjet 100 aircraft, Aeroflot signed a letter of intent for a further 20 of the aircraft, announced in 2015.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136">
        <a href="#cite_note-136">
         [135]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Aeroflot retired its three McDonnell Douglas MD-11 freighters from active service in July 2013
       <span style="display:none">
        (
        <span class="dtend">
         2013-07
        </span>
        )
       </span>
       citing their operation as no longer profitable.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_ends_MD-11_freighter_operations_137-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_ends_MD-11_freighter_operations-137">
         [136]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2015 the company expanded its fleet with three Boeing 777-300ERs, six 737-800s and four Sukhoi Superjets; and retired five Ilyushin Il-96s.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138">
        <a href="#cite_note-138">
         [137]
        </a>
       </sup>
       During the
       <a href="/wiki/Paris_Air_Show" title="Paris Air Show">
        2015 Paris Air Show
       </a>
       , Aeroflot cancelled an order for 22
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/787_Dreamliner" title="787 Dreamliner">
        Boeing 787 Dreamliners
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PARIS:_Aeroflot_cancels_787_order_121-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-PARIS:_Aeroflot_cancels_787_order-121">
         [120]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In mid-2016 a deal for a further 10 leased Sukhoi Superjets was announced.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139">
        <a href="#cite_note-139">
         [138]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In November 2016, Aeroflot cancelled eight Airbus A350-800s from an order including these aircraft and 14 A350-900s and also announced that its cancelled
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/787_Dreamliner" title="787 Dreamliner">
        Boeing 787
       </a>
       order would be transferred to
       <a href="/wiki/Rostec" title="Rostec">
        Rostec
       </a>
       subsidiary
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Avia_Capital_Services&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Avia Capital Services (page does not exist)">
        Avia Capital Services
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_cancels_eight_A350-800s_3-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_cancels_eight_A350-800s-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_transfers_787_deal_to_Avia_Capital_Services_140-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_transfers_787_deal_to_Avia_Capital_Services-140">
         [139]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141">
        <a href="#cite_note-141">
         [140]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Aeroflot firmed up an order for 20 Sukhoi Superjet 100s in July 2017 during the
       <a href="/wiki/MAKS_Air_Show" title="MAKS Air Show">
        MAKS Air Show
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aeroflot_firms_order_for_20_SSJ100s_142-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aeroflot_firms_order_for_20_SSJ100s-142">
         [141]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On 31 August 2017, Aeroflot Group approved plans to purchase additional 6 new Boeing 777-300ER to significantly strengthen the long-haul capabilities of its fleet. Deliveries of the aircraft are scheduled from 2Q 2018 to 1Q 2019.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143">
        <a href="#cite_note-143">
         [142]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144">
        <a href="#cite_note-144">
         [143]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Current">
        Current
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Aeroflot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Current">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aeroflot_A321-200_VP-BWN_SVO_Jun_2011.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1200" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Aeroflot_A321-200_VP-BWN_SVO_Jun_2011.png/220px-Aeroflot_A321-200_VP-BWN_SVO_Jun_2011.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Aeroflot_A321-200_VP-BWN_SVO_Jun_2011.png/330px-Aeroflot_A321-200_VP-BWN_SVO_Jun_2011.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Aeroflot_A321-200_VP-BWN_SVO_Jun_2011.png/440px-Aeroflot_A321-200_VP-BWN_SVO_Jun_2011.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aeroflot_A321-200_VP-BWN_SVO_Jun_2011.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         An Aeroflot
         <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A321" title="Airbus A321">
          Airbus A321-200
         </a>
         just departed from Sheremetyevo Airport in 2011.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Boeing_737-8LJ,_Aeroflot_JP7740981.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1200" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Boeing_737-8LJ%2C_Aeroflot_JP7740981.jpg/220px-Boeing_737-8LJ%2C_Aeroflot_JP7740981.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Boeing_737-8LJ%2C_Aeroflot_JP7740981.jpg/330px-Boeing_737-8LJ%2C_Aeroflot_JP7740981.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Boeing_737-8LJ%2C_Aeroflot_JP7740981.jpg/440px-Boeing_737-8LJ%2C_Aeroflot_JP7740981.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Boeing_737-8LJ,_Aeroflot_JP7740981.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         An Aeroflot
         <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_Next_Generation" title="Boeing 737 Next Generation">
          Boeing 737-800
         </a>
         on approach to
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sheremetyevo_Airport" title="Sheremetyevo Airport">
          Sheremetyevo Airport
         </a>
         in 2013.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       For most of its history, Aeroflot's fleet consisted entirely of aircraft built by Soviet manufacturers
       <a href="/wiki/Antonov" title="Antonov">
        Antonov
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ilyushin" title="Ilyushin">
        Ilyushin
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Tupolev" title="Tupolev">
        Tupolev
       </a>
       . Following the Soviet Union's dissolution and subsequent partition of the airline, Aeroflot began replacing its old Soviet aircraft with Western and modern Russian models.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Aeroflot fleet comprises the following aircraft (as of February 2018
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Aeroflot&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       ):
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PlanePark_145-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-PlanePark-145">
         [144]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
